<div id="review_1004038533" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1004038533" />
    <a title="Deanna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4996519-deanna"><img alt="Deanna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1431289860p2/4996519.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1004038533?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deanna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deanna" href="/user/show/4996519-deanna">Deanna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4996519-deanna?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4996519-deanna?shelf=shitty">shitty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4996519-deanna?shelf=boring">boring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4996519-deanna?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4996519-deanna?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4996519-deanna?shelf=bullshit-of-the-century">bullshit-of-the-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4996519-deanna?shelf=pissed-me-off-so-much">pissed-me-off-so-much</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1004038533" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18267488030299955071">2.5 stars. <br/>Reposting my review.<br/><br/>Every year, 8 girls get listed as the "ugliest" or the "prettiest" girl of their year.<br/>For this years prettiest, we have freshman Abby Warner, sophomore Lauren Finn, junior Bridget Honeycutt, and senior Margo Gable.<br/>For the ugliest, we have freshman Danielle Demarco, Candace Kincaid, Sarah Singer, and Jennifer Briggis (who's been listed as the ugliest for the last three years as well, making her the only student who has been listed all four years).<br/><br/>The story happens o</span>
  <span id="freeText18267488030299955071" style="display:none">2.5 stars. <br />Reposting my review.<br /><br />Every year, 8 girls get listed as the "ugliest" or the "prettiest" girl of their year.<br />For this years prettiest, we have freshman Abby Warner, sophomore Lauren Finn, junior Bridget Honeycutt, and senior Margo Gable.<br />For the ugliest, we have freshman Danielle Demarco, Candace Kincaid, Sarah Singer, and Jennifer Briggis (who's been listed as the ugliest for the last three years as well, making her the only student who has been listed all four years).<br /><br />The story happens over a span of six days, following the eight different girls and how the list has affected them.<br /><br />For Abby, ever since the list came out and listed her as the prettiest (and for overcoming family genetics), her older sister has been distant. While the two sisters have always been so different [her older sister being scholastic and Abby being rather materialistic], they still were on good terms with her. That was before the list comes out.<br /><br />For Danielle Demarco, the list has a negative effect on her. She was labeled the ugliest (and called "Dan the Man"), which only ends up having a negative effect on her insecurity.<br />I, right off the bat, felt sympathetic towards Danielle (and the other "uglies") because no girl should ever be called the ugliest of her year, and then be ridiculed for her features. Danielle is athletic, really strong, and is really muscular. [However, when you read the book, you'll later find out that she was listed as the ugliest for an even dumber reason. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[: because she has a boyfriend and has a little PDA with him every now and then, and the person who made the list was obviously jealous and annoyed with the fact that Danielle and her boyfriend, Andrew, actually did something couples do: make out <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />When Danielle was listed ugliest, it all goes sour for her. Her relationship with her boyfriend (from camp) becomes distant and she became too fixated on trying to understand why she was on the list and why her boyfriend was distant, rather than her swim.<br /><br />For sophomore ugliest, we have Candace Kincaid. She's not ugly on the outside, but she is on the inside. While the first chapter that she was introduced in showed how "shallow" she is, I never truly understood why her friends were so quick to complain to others that she was so "mean" and insufferable. Shallow, yes. Ugly on the inside? Not really.<br />In the span of the book, her arc demonstrates that she's not that bad of a person. (By the end of the book, I really liked how far her character developed).<br /><br />For sophomore's prettiest, we have Lauren Finn (listed and described with "everyone's hot for the new girl"). Having been homeschooled, Lauren didn't have that many friends. It doesn't help that her mother is extremely protective (and that she calls her mother "mommy"). Her grandfather has died, leaving her mother and her a house to live in.<br />While I didn't mind Lauren's character often, I minded her mother a lot. She was controlling, made too many quick assumptions, evasive and was too close-minded.<br />By the end of Lauren's arc, I found myself annoyed with how it ended for her. Her character arc was the one that needed most improvement.<br /><br />For junior's ugliest, we have rebel Sarah Singer. Pissed that she's on the list (not because she cares about the list, but because at this time, she's insecure about her boyfriend and his ex-girlfriend), she decides to prove to the school that she can get uglier by not showering at all and wearing the same clothes everyday. I felt sympathetic for Sarah (as I did for Danielle) because she was insecure when it comes to her boyfriend, and the list just made it so much worse. [Spoiler: she was listed because the girl who listed her hated her rebel, tough girl act and wanted to call her out on it.]<br /><br />For junior's prettiest, we have Bridget Honeycutt. Having been slightly overweight, she ends up with an eating disorder over the summer after trying on a swim suit and, to her horror, finds out it does not fit her. Too ashamed to not put it back (and because her mother's impatiently waiting for her), she buys it. She ended up starving herself, running whenever she gets hungry--and by the time she came back to school, she's skinny.<br />The list doesn't really impact her life, because she was more fixated on her weight (something her sister, who's best friend with freshman's prettiest, is worried over). She ends up trying random cleanses in hopes of losing even more weight before Homecoming. She then decides that starving herself would be an even better method, cause then there would be nothing to have to worry about.<br />This ends up with a falling out between her and her sister, and that's how her arc ends.<br />In another character's chapter, she talks to Bridget, who's too sad at Homecoming over her sister's annoyance at her. The list had little to do with her eating disorder, but the chapter had it as if the list is the reason that caused her falling out with her sister.<br /><br />For senior's ugliest, we have Jennifer Briggis. She's the only girl who has won the ugliest for the last three years. With that kind of record, you (the audience/readers) are supposed to feel sorry for her.<br />Right off the bat, she takes the label with pride. It mentions how the first year (freshman year), when she found out she was humiliated and ungracefully reacted (crying, wailing, flailing, throwing up, the works). I felt sympathetic for her then, but that was it. She was making a scene over something very shallow and trivial. She had friends (girls from choir) of her own, but she always thought she was prettier than them, superior than them, better than them, the works.<br />That's when my sympathy for the character ended.<br />We later learn that she's overweight and used to be good friends with senior's prettiest, Margo Gamble.<br />This is a character you wanted to feel sympathetic for--but as the story progresses, you realize how she shouldn't have won "ugliest" for her looks. She should have won it for her ugly personality [her ugly personality tops Candace's]. Margo's two best friends take sympathy on her, and decides to try to help campaign for her to win homecoming queen.<br />They invite her to a pre-homecoming party (for Jennifer's behalf) at Margo's house, where she proves to be as terrible as ever as she "pretends" to go to the bathroom and then goes into Margo's room and tries to find her diary. [You learn throughout the book from Margo's perspective chapters that she stopped being friends with Jennifer because of how clingy and obsessive Jen was towards her, and how Jen always made her feel so bad about herself]. We then learn that Jennifer, throughout her life, has always read Margo's diary in order to put Margo "back in her place" whenever she was "out of line."<br />I stopped feeling sorry for her. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[[Spoilers: you later learn that she's the one in charge of this year's list, and has used terrible reasons to justify why certain people deserved to be on the list. You also learn to not like her because not only did her character not develop, it backtracked.] <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> She got so petty over the hopes of winning homecoming queen (as a way to stick it to her ex-friend, Margo) she goes running to the principal when she hears that Sarah (Junior's ugliest) might pull some type of stunt at the homecoming dance.<br /><br />Margo Gable was senior's prettiest. While she was slightly shallow at some times, she was a sympathetic character. Her best friends, Dana and Rachel, were too busy feeling sorry over Jennifer (painting Jen as the innocent victim, while Margo was painted as the villain). She had a strained relationship with her older sister. She still feels guilty for cutting Jennifer out of her life, but reasoned it was for the best--because of Jennifer's obsession with Margo. She even calls herself out on it in front of her friends, which was something that made me realize that she's not really a mean girl.<br /><br />Overall, the story's pacing is slow and all over the place (as it follows eight different character). While we, the readers, find out who is the one behind this year's list (and the previous few years), we never ever get to see the principal or other girls (sans Margo) find out who created this year's list. Too many endings are left ambiguous, some more painfully obvious than others.<br /><br />This book had a great concept but a poor execution.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18267488030299955071" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_910282698" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/910282698" />
    <a title="Drew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22104588-drew"><img alt="Drew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498412758p2/22104588.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/910282698?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Drew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Drew" href="/user/show/22104588-drew">Drew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22104588-drew?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22104588-drew?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer910282698" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer311386954118453860">2 1/2 stars. I think this is one of those cases where <b>the author bit off more than she could chew.</b><br/><br/>Let's start with the positive. I really appreciated the diversity and the examination of different kinds of girls in school. There were airheads, mean girls, ones with pent-up anger, and genuinely nice girls. This book showed girls under the pressure of their cliques to maintain a perfect image, girls hiding their problems behind a beautiful smile, and worst of all - jealousy, guilt, and betrayal. <b>I</b></span>
  <span id="freeText311386954118453860" style="display:none">2 1/2 stars. I think this is one of those cases where <b>the author bit off more than she could chew.</b><br /><br />Let's start with the positive. I really appreciated the diversity and the examination of different kinds of girls in school. There were airheads, mean girls, ones with pent-up anger, and genuinely nice girls. This book showed girls under the pressure of their cliques to maintain a perfect image, girls hiding their problems behind a beautiful smile, and worst of all - jealousy, guilt, and betrayal. <b>It was a whirlwind of drama.</b><br /><br />The basic summary is that a list goes around every year and on it are the names of the prettiest and ugliest girls in school. Some of the girls are surprised where their names end up and the twisted tradition, unsurprisingly, causes a lot of problems.<br /><br />The leader of a popular group, Cadence, starts questioning how nice she really is when the list names her "ugliest on the inside," Danielle's doubts toward her boyfriend grow when he doesn't stick up for her after she is nominated ugliest, and Bridget's eating disorder she has struggled to overcome last year flares back up.<br /><br />So many different problems were looked at - money issues at home, sister rivalries, bad boyfriends, fake friends, and body image issues. I thought the author did a great job at digging into each of these girls' minds and laying out all their thoughts for the reader to understand and sympathize with.<br /><br />When I started this book I thought it could easily be four star material, for the plot and narratives were set up perfectly. What could go wrong? But it gradually became apparent that the author missed a lot of potential when, near the end of the book, I realized <b>the plot wasn't going anywhere.</b><br /><br />Sadly, many of the issues the girls were dealing with weren't resolved by the end. This may have been an attempt to make things more realistic - the anorexic girl was still unhappy with her body at the end? Deal with it. But the lack of conclusion made the rest of the story feel kind of pointless.<br /><br />The writing was entertaining and I thought this was an interesting experiment, but to me it felt like <b>the author took on more than she could handle.</b> With a more mindful plot and a carefully executed ending, this could have been a very important book.<br /><br />I would have liked to see a stronger message about how outside beauty doesn't matter, and it's people's dynamic, sparkling personalities that really count. But in <i>The List</i> the gorgeous mean girls blended in with the truly kind-hearted ones and I felt like a huge and powerful point had been missed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="311386954118453860" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2117841041" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2117841041" />
    <a title="Fuzaila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55299343-fuzaila"><img alt="Fuzaila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532881347p2/55299343.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2117841041?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fuzaila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fuzaila" href="/user/show/55299343-fuzaila">Fuzaila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=drama-overloaded">drama-overloaded</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=romance-lovey-dovey">romance-lovey-dovey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=school-boarding-genres">school-boarding-genres</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2117841041" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6472936225516576818">This book was a different take on high school contemporary. An original plot, memorable characters, and quick pace, made it a delectable read. Being a <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/151371.Jenny_Han' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jenny Han</a> fan, I’ve been meaning to read Siobhan Vivian for a long time now, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10866233-the-list?from_search=true' rel='nofollow noopener'>The List</a> certainly made me want to discover more of the author. <b>3.5/5 stars.</b><br/><br/><u>THE PLOT</u><br/><br/>A week before the homecoming dance, the students of Mount Washington High come to school to find a list taped and stapled to doors, lockers, notice boards and everywhere else. It isn’t som</span>
  <span id="freeText6472936225516576818" style="display:none">This book was a different take on high school contemporary. An original plot, memorable characters, and quick pace, made it a delectable read. Being a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/151371.Jenny_Han" rel="nofollow noopener">Jenny Han</a> fan, I’ve been meaning to read Siobhan Vivian for a long time now, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10866233-the-list?from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">The List</a> certainly made me want to discover more of the author. <b>3.5/5 stars.</b><br /><br /><u>THE PLOT</u><br /><br />A week before the homecoming dance, the students of Mount Washington High come to school to find a list taped and stapled to doors, lockers, notice boards and everywhere else. It isn’t something extraordinary, just a list declaring the prettiest and the ugliest girl in each year, except, it IS a big deal. No one knows who prepares the list; it has been a tradition for so long. This year, eight girls find themselves in spotlight after the list is published. <br /><br /><b>Abby Warner</b> - a clueless freshman, looking forward to have an enjoyable high school period. Like all girls her age, she wants to look pretty, impress boys and be admired. The list only helps her cause, or so she thinks.<br /><br /><b>Danielle DeMarco</b> - highly talented swimmer; selected to the varsity team. The list does nothing to her confidence, but not everyone else is pacified with her indifference – including her boyfriend.<br /><br /><b>Candace Kincaid</b> - She knows she is pretty, and so does everyone else. And yet the list naming her the ugliest sophomore makes everyone to reconsider their beauty standards and in turn, Candace finds herself abandoned by her closest friends.<br /><br /><b>Lauren Finn</b> - Being homeschooled, Lauren has no much idea about school and friends. UNTIL THE LIST HAPPENED. Being the prettiest sophomore, a bunch of girls are suddenly eager for her friendship. Lauren has to figure out who’s earnest and who’s not.<br /><br /><b>Sarah Singer</b> - When the list pronounces that she is trying to be as ugly as possible, Sarah becomes determined to meet their expectations and show them how ugly actually looks like. But how good is her façade?<br /><br /><b>Bridget Honeycutt</b> - Being on the list was hard work, and even harder is maintaining her title of the prettiest girl. The constant need to eat coincides with a desperation to prove the list right, and Bridget must make sure not to stagger under the pressure.<br /><br /><b>Jennifer Briggis</b> - Being the ugliest for four years, Jennifer has developed an immunity to the list and unexpectedly, draws pity from others. People hail her for her bravery and even go as far as to nominate her for homecoming queen – Jennifer doesn’t mind the attention. <br /><br /><b>Margo Gable</b> - Becoming the homecoming queen was a given for Margo. Being the prettiest senior also strengthens her chances. But Jennifer has a fan base of her own too. Uncovering a secret and being guilty of one of her own, Margo finds herself in the midst of confusion and betrayal.<br /><br />	<br /><b>The book is narrated in eight povs.</b> Yeah, you heard that right – 8 povs. Most of the books can’t even properly deal with a single character, but here Siobhan Vivian has done a splendid job by offering each girl’s perspectives with stunning clearness. There wasn’t a single moment when I got the names and characters all tangled up. Even with all the characters and all the issues it deals with, the book isn’t messy. <br /><br /><b>The characters also have a lot of depth in them.</b> Each girl is unique in her own way and seem <b>very real. <br /><br />DISCLAIMER: There is a lot of body-shaming in this book. Like, in every chapter. It also deals with eating disorder. </b> But, these themes are just a part of the drama and does not try to overpower the book.<br /><br />I am amazed by how perfectly Vivian has captured the emotions and feelings of each of the characters. Sarah’s attitude, Danielle’s mask-face, Bridget’s turmoil, Lauren’s mindset, every other character has been given particular characteristics and they’re portrayed in a very symbolic way. <br /><br /><b>But, the book is not without it’s flaws</b>. Some of the characters were given so little time of appearance, that somewhat diminishes their significance in the story. For example, Candace is indicated to be a bad person, but we do not get any clarifications or explanations or flashbacks of any sort. <b>The whole book seems incomplete.</b> <br />There were MANY THINGS that were not explained. It affects the way readers connect to the characters. <br /><br />And HOW ABSURD WAS THAT ENDING? I seriously thought my book was missing pages. It was as if the author was rushing to meet a deadline to finish the book and in the process forgot to clarify what was to be the end of the story. I mean how do you deal with something so.. <i>incomplete</i>?? Like, what happened to Sarah? Was Lauren able to convince her mom? What about Abby? Daniel? Did Candace have a change of mind? And what about Jennifer? How did they all deal with those things? So many questions! And not a glimpse of an answer -.-<br /><br /><b>Overall, </b> the book doesn’t end on a completely positive note, which was what I expected. With all the themes addressed here, in the end they felt scattered, lay about. I really wish the author had bothered to give some more insight, a personal touch to the whole thing.<br /> Either way, if you love contemporaries, chick-lit, and lots of high-school drama, then this book is for you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6472936225516576818" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Many of the minor characters weren't even named, they were, "her friend from science class" or some other descriptor that didn't include a name. That made me feel like the author didn't really care either. This has been on my "currently reading" list long enough. It's time to move it onto my DNF list. <br/><br/>Not my cup of tea. Others may enjoy, but I just couldn't get </span>
  <span id="freeText1311209946991832359" style="display:none">Meh. This one just didn't do it for me. I only got about 104 pages into it and just don't really care about the characters or the plot. Many of the minor characters weren't even named, they were, "her friend from science class" or some other descriptor that didn't include a name. That made me feel like the author didn't really care either. This has been on my "currently reading" list long enough. It's time to move it onto my DNF list. <br /><br />Not my cup of tea. Others may enjoy, but I just couldn't get into it. Two stars, because while I'm not finishing it, it's not due to anger or poor writing. It's just kind of blah.</span>

<div id="review_2772404451" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2772404451" />
    <a title="❤Amy and Sofie❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/92592776-amy-and-sofie"><img alt="❤Amy and Sofie❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596967015p2/92592776.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2772404451?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="❤Amy and Sofie❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="❤Amy and Sofie❤ " href="/user/show/92592776-amy-and-sofie">❤Amy and Sofie❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28600522-the-list">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/92592776-amy-and-sofie?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/92592776-amy-and-sofie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2772404451" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6993973879352598108">First of all, wow.<br/><br/>This book was so.. what's the word.. Teenage! Suited me so much. It deserves my 4 stars! <br/><br/>I wanted to know who wrote the list. If they didn't reveal who did I wouldn't have given it 4 stars.<br/><br/>There were 2 girls for each grade. And eight girls on the list altogether. <br/><br/>My favourite was probably Margo Gable. She was the prettiest senior. She used to be pals with Jennifer Briggis until they fell apart in eight grade. Now Jennifer has come back and now Margos chance for homecoming queen</span>
  <span id="freeText6993973879352598108" style="display:none">First of all, wow.<br /><br />This book was so.. what's the word.. Teenage! Suited me so much. It deserves my 4 stars! <br /><br />I wanted to know who wrote the list. If they didn't reveal who did I wouldn't have given it 4 stars.<br /><br />There were 2 girls for each grade. And eight girls on the list altogether. <br /><br />My favourite was probably Margo Gable. She was the prettiest senior. She used to be pals with Jennifer Briggis until they fell apart in eight grade. Now Jennifer has come back and now Margos chance for homecoming queen might be ruined. <br /><br />I hated Sarah Singer until the end, when I learned to love her. She planned on ruining everything and her story was disgusting. But at the end I learned to love her for a reason.<br /><br />I felt really mad at Fern, Abby Warner the pretty freshman's sister. I won't say why, it will spoil it.<br />In my mind, I pictured Abbby as a beautiful girl who many boys would want to date. I liked her story too. Her and BFF Lisa love talking about cute boys and falling on love. Like me. Typical teen girl stuff. Abbys sister Fern is weird. She hangs about teachers and all. Odd. After being on the list some boys did ask Abby out. List suckers!<br /><br />I liked Danielle Demarco as well. She ended up being ugly. And her boyfriend's pals teased her. She and her boyfriend end up falling out. I liked Danielles style the most.<br /><br />Lauren Finn was horrible. I hated her the most. At the start I thought she was lovely but then she turned out to be a drunk stupid freak. I hated her choices she made to all those girls and Candace.<br /><br />Now speaking of Canace. Candace Kincaid was great. At first I thought she was that Instagram make up beauty kid but no! She helped Lauren ( why?????) And became a socialite outcast.<br /><br />Finally Bridget Honneycutt. Bridget worried about weight after some certain discovery. She works hard to lose weight and after all the hard work, gets named prettiest. But she fights with lisa and still keeps trying to reduce weight. She finally does enough to suit her and has a great homecoming. <br /><br />Last of all, ( I promise!) Is Jennifer Briggis. 4 years in a row ugly! Wow. Poor girl. Jennifer is getting treated nicely this year though. But with Margo, not cool girl.<br />Jennifer hides a big secret Margo is shocked to hear.<br /><br />Want to know the secret so much, read the book! <br /><br />This was one of the most Epic teenage reads I've read in ages. I think I'll read more Siobhan Vivian sometime. Give this a read.<br /><br />Age group reccomendation: 13 to any other age. <br />I don't think younger kids should read this. They wouldn't understand all the romance and feelings. <br /><br />❤❤❤❤❤❤❤❤❤❤❤❤❤❤❤❤❤❤❤❤🙊🙊🙊😗😚</span>

<div id="review_603061277" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/603061277" />
    <a title="Jackie &quot;the Librarian&quot;" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/289556-jackie-the-librarian"><img alt="Jackie &quot;the Librarian&quot;" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307387831p2/289556.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/603061277?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jackie &quot;the Librarian&quot;" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jackie &quot;the Librarian&quot;" href="/user/show/289556-jackie-the-librarian">Jackie &quot;the Librarian&quot;</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/289556-jackie-the-librarian?shelf=youngadult">youngadult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/289556-jackie-the-librarian?shelf=misery-oh-misery">misery-oh-misery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer603061277" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15035287145913494859">Do you remember what you looked like in high school? No, wait… not how you actually looked, but how you felt like you looked. Even if you looked okay, you didn’t necessarily <i>feel</i> like you did. And worrying about everyone looking at you, judging you, that horrible self-consciousness that scars you for THE REST OF YOUR LIFE. <br/>Okay, maybe I'm being a little overdramatic, but this is a book about teenagers, and that's what it feels like when you're a teen. <br/><br/>And truly, high school sucks. No, I don’t me</span>
  <span id="freeText15035287145913494859" style="display:none">Do you remember what you looked like in high school? No, wait… not how you actually looked, but how you felt like you looked. Even if you looked okay, you didn’t necessarily <i>feel</i> like you did. And worrying about everyone looking at you, judging you, that horrible self-consciousness that scars you for THE REST OF YOUR LIFE. <br />Okay, maybe I'm being a little overdramatic, but this is a book about teenagers, and that's what it feels like when you're a teen. <br /><br />And truly, high school sucks. No, I don’t mean it’s full of vampires (not in this book, anyways). It’s hell, yes, but not literally. Trapped in a judgmental fishbowl with hormone bombs who don’t want to be there, yippee. Now imagine if on top of the usual hell, there’s A LIST that comes out every year listing the prettiest and the ugliest girl from each grade. (Why not boys, too, I wonder? Not fair!)<br /><br />In this book, eight girls are singled out for attention by being named either the prettiest or the ugliest in their grade in high school. Who makes the list, no one knows. Drama! Mystery! I sucked this book down so fast that if it had been a milkshake I would have gotten an ice cream headache. I am SO grateful my high school didn’t have this tradition. To be singled out based on some secret committee’s opinion of one’s appearance (or behavior, in one girl’s case) is a horrific thought. <br /><br />Each girl had a story, but we only got to know a little about each of them. I wanted to know way more. But the main question raised was not: <i>who makes the list?</i> although that was covered. No, the real question is what makes a person beautiful, and what makes a person ugly. And what about inner beauty? Don’t forget about that! <br /><br />Not great literature, no, but it worked for me. This would be a great teen book group book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15035287145913494859" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10165983-ellis?shelf=lolwhut">lolwhut</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10165983-ellis?shelf=own-physical-copy">own-physical-copy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer920961380" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17706547180067497259">I'm not entirely sure what exactly I expected to get from <i>The List</i>, but I ended up quite disappointed anyway. Don't get me wrong. This is a very readable book with a nice story that moves at a quick pace, but I really slogged through some of the chapters, mostly because there were certain characters I just couldn't stand. The beginning was rough and I initially thought the writing quite juvenile, though it later became clear that this was more a reflection of the character in question than the w</span>
  <span id="freeText17706547180067497259" style="display:none">I'm not entirely sure what exactly I expected to get from <i>The List</i>, but I ended up quite disappointed anyway. Don't get me wrong. This is a very readable book with a nice story that moves at a quick pace, but I really slogged through some of the chapters, mostly because there were certain characters I just couldn't stand. The beginning was rough and I initially thought the writing quite juvenile, though it later became clear that this was more a reflection of the character in question than the writing itself, which is always a plus in my book. <br /><br />I think part of my puzzlement has to do with the format of this novel. Maybe it's because I've been reading so many short story collections for my English lit class lately, but this read more like a series of snapshots than a traditionally, fully plotted-out novel. This isn't a bad thing per se, and I like how open and ambiguous the ending is, especially considering the time frame only spans a week. However, I also think that this division in days of the week in combination with their respective subdivision into small chapters, where each chapter belongs to a different character, gives the whole a rather disjointed feel. I'm sorry for the confusion these last few sentences might have induced. On the plus side, we're now on an equal level of "trying to make sense of dis". <br /><br /><br />Read the rest on <a href="http://randomtransliterator.blogspot.be/2014/05/review-list.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Random Transliterator</a>. </span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('m1t7iA3FMrE4X5Uragz3QbT1XuMN0xJcGQopWkSZ+DSZCkVfsyOtrocqHq6itQUSiHP94g+CDUiooPKHaXxvxw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kkyYAWJ7g8SElw2SLqKuxNNYvFTpudUiZy5C0jA6iF2QHabW3J0c2zvihhfmG1yX794fVevoyjbWhJkPHd8frg==')})
  }

Between the rumors about the fight he was in (and that brief stint in juvie that followed it) and his reputation as a loner, he\'s not exactly the ideal person to be stuck with. Still, she just keeps reminding herself that it is only a matter of time before Jeff, her almost-boyfriend, realizes he left her in the library and comes to rescue her.\n\nOnly he doesn\'t come. No one does.\n\nInstead it becomes clear that Autumn is going to have to spend the next couple of days living off vending-machine food and making conversation with a boy who clearly wants nothing to do with her. Except there is more to Dax than meets the eye.\n\nAs he and Autumn at first grudgingly, and then not so grudgingly, open up to each other, Autumn is struck by their surprising connection. But can their feelings for each other survive once the weekend is over and Autumn\'s old life, and old love interest, threaten to pull her from Dax\'s side?<\/span>\n  <a <span id="freeTextContainer1355636017573894058">Siobhan Vivian is the author of THE LAST BOY AND GIRL IN THE WORLD (April 2016), as well as THE LIST, NOT THAT KIND OF GIRL, SAME DIFFERENCE, and A LITTLE FRIENDLY ADVICE. She also co-wrote BURN FOR BURN series with her best friend JENNY HAN. She currently lives in Pittsburgh. </span>
